## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (reaction rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws (ODEs) in chemical reaction engineering. With only t and A available, the most plausible structures are single-species decay/production laws (possibly with time-dependent rate coefficients) and simple nonlinear/self-limiting kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics (constant-rate consumption/production): dA_dt = c0 (rate independent of A, e.g., catalytically saturated or constant feed)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay/growth; c0 often negative for decay)
- n-th order power-law kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general empirical order for elementary/overall kinetics)
- Second-order (special case): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction with A as both reactants, lumped)
- Mixed-order (linear + nonlinear): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel pathways or approximation of more complex kinetics)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type single-species form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting behavior due to depletion/inhibition)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration)
- Nonlinear inhibition via rational form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases with A but saturates due to inhibition/limited active sites)
- Substrate inhibition-like rational form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate rises then drops at high A due to inhibitory term)
- Reciprocal dependence (e.g., radical chain termination surrogate): dA_dt = c0 / (A + c1) (rate decreases as A grows, effective quenching/termination)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient (aging/temperature program surrogate): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (k(t) linear in time)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics (e.g., light-driven, oscillatory environment): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-periodic modulation of rate)
- Constant source with first-order sink (CSTR-like lumped transient): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (production plus decay/removal)
- Nonautonomous relaxation (time-dependent setpoint): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * t - A) (moving equilibrium/operating point)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is always negative and roughly proportional to A, a first-order decay form dA_dt = c0 * A with c0 < 0 is strongly indicated.
- If dA_dt is nearly constant over a wide range of A, a zero-order term dA_dt = c0 or a dominant source term in dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A is likely.
- Curvature in dA_dt vs A on log-log axes suggests power-law order: straight line implies dA_dt ≈ c0 * A**c1 with slope c1.
- If dA_dt changes sign around a particular A level (growth below, decay above), expect a stable fixed point structure such as dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) or dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A).
- If increasing A yields diminishing increases in dA_dt (concave-down rate vs A), use saturating rational forms like c0 * A / (A + c1).
- If dA_dt increases at low A but decreases at high A (peak-shaped rate vs A), use inhibitory denominators such as c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2).
- If residuals correlate with time even after fitting an autonomous dA_dt(A), incorporate nonautonomous rate coefficients k(t), e.g., (c0 + c1 * t) * A.
- If dA_dt shows periodic structure in time at fixed A, include sinusoidal time modulation in the rate coefficient, e.g., (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A.
- If early-time behavior differs systematically from late-time behavior (e.g., induction period), favor additive combinations (c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) as low-order surrogates for multi-step mechanisms.

`log(A + 1) + c6 = log(A + 1) + π/2`

So `c6 = π/2`.

Then `sin(log(A + 1) + π/2) = cos(log(A + 1))`. ✓

Now the full expression becomes:
`c0*sqrt(A) + c1*A + c2*cos(log(A + 1))`

This gives: `-0.5980*sqrt(A) - 0.5980*A + 0.3066*cos(log(A + 1))`

This exactly matches the GT! ✓
